I dont want to be that practitioner. Its myopic at best and dishonest and potentially harmful at worst. We dedicated July to uterine health - and the same thing applies here - there is NO ONE solution. But, there ARE solutions. To deal with the stubborn involuntary incontinence, I had to use a topical DHEA (to strengthen the muscles down there) and learn to sit on a ball (to release the fascia and bring blood flow to the area). The main uterine changes women experience in perimenopause and menopause are: Involuntary incontinence Vaginal infections: BV, candida, and UTIs Abnormal growth: Fibroids, uterine polyps, and PMS Vaginal atrophy: Thinning, pain, sensitivity, and burning sensation down thereThe key underlying causes for these changes are: Declining estrogen levels Declining progesterone levels Declining DHEA/testosterone levels Bacterial changes Weakened pelvic floor (due to poor fascia, birthing, and age)What are the solutions? 1. For declining estrogen levels Correct the estrogen levels (and balance with progesterone) by trying [Wise Womens Balance](https://wellena.com/products/wise-womens-balance-1?_pos=1&_sid=a6269ac80&_ss=r) - formulated with phytoestrogens (gentle, naturally-occurring estrogens) - or the [Estrogen Boost](https://wellena.com/products/estrogen-boost?_pos=1&_sid=9d18857d8&_ss=r) - contains hops and Norwegian spruce, which are both potent phytoestrogens. If herbs dont work for you, get bioidentical estrogen (cream, patches) - work with a skilled BHRT (bioidentical hormone replacement therapy) practitioner. 2. If you want to explore systemic raise of DHEA levels, work with a BHRT (bioidentical hormone replacement therapy) practitioner. 4. For bacterial changes (BV, UTIs, candida)Correcting estrogen levels may help correct these infections in the long run. For a quicker relief, consider our new [She-Biotics](https://wellena.com/products/she-biotics?_pos=1&_sid=5fec5c18d&_ss=r) - we formulated it to contain 4 strains of Lactobacillus that research shows impressive results when dealing with vaginal infections. While dealing with a vaginal infection, be sure to keep an anti-inflammatory diet, and [completely] lay off alcohol and any form of sugar (including fruit). 5. For a weakened pelvic floor (leaking, pain, thinning)Consider the [Coochball](https://www.bloombetter.life/WELLENA). I never fully understood and appreciated the power of the fascia, muscle tone, and blood supply to the pelvic area and how it impacts our posture, organ health, etc - until I met Jana Danielson (the creator of the Coochball). When you get the Coochball, you will also get access to her exercises showing how to best use the ball (this is only for our community). MagdalenaP.S.
